  49. In reviewing this product, I first provide a caveat - I've never used a cordless razor before as I have partial to the traditional blade and foam. With that being said...<br /><br />Appearance [4/5]: The razor gets a four out of five for appearance because of its smooth sleek no frills look. It's a razor and looks just like one. It was a detail trimmer on the back and three rotating blades up front. It's texture provides for a good grip (which is great if you use it in the shower) and it appears to be designed with simplicity in mind. The only reason it didn't get a five is that it looked a little too simple. For a razor in this price range, I would expect a little more.<br /><br />Features [4/5]: The razor gets a four out of five because I feel it has two major flaws. First, the detail trimmer blade is pretty useless. I've used similar style detail blades before and this one isn't nearly as sharp or nearly as power. You kind of have to apply a bit more force or get in closer than you desire - which completely defeats the point of having a detail trimmer as you can essentially ruin the style you are aiming for. Also, the fact that it comes with a charging cable as opposed to a stand was kind of a letdown. I would have expected a cordless razor to be just that. But this isn't a real negative, just a personal qualm with it. One of the better features is the quick charge function. If you are in need of a quick shave and have forgotten to charge the unit, a quick five minute charge will give you two to three minutes of use - which is great if you are just touching up or getting rid of some shadow.<br /><br />Use/Functionality [4/5]: This also gets a four. A huge part of this is the fact that its waterproof (as it should be) which allows it to be used in the shower. However (maybe it's just because I take showers at near scalding temperatures), blades usually move smoother in warmer environments but this one sometimes sticks to my skin if it's too hot. On the other hand,in a completely dry environment, it cuts just as smooth as it would in (non-scalding) water so I guess that makes up for it. The cut is fairly close (depends on how thick your hair is) and I only needed minimal touch ups with a blade after using the shaver. Clean-up is a breeze as you literally flick open the blade assembly, rinse, and close. Battery life is decent (could be longer I think) but then again it does charge fairly quickly.<br /><br />Overall [4/5]: Aside from the poor detail trimmer, average battery life, and lack of a charging station this is a pretty solid razor. I would like to see these issues addressed in subsequent models but aside from these annoyances, I find the razor overall to be a pretty good product.

  197. Philips models AT830 and 6948XL are among the most useful of current rotary shavers. Both have articulated cutting heads in 3-head assemblies that are imbedded in shaver bodies rather than in floating holders. Both have internal batteries and wide, pop-up trimmers. Neither comes with a charging stand. A battery charge is rated to provide 50 minutes use with model AT830 and 35 minutes use with model 6948XL.<br /><br />Intermediate-priced model AT830 has a lithium-ion battery, has cutting heads mounted in a rocking holder and is waterproof, allowing wet shaving. It comes with an external 15 volt, 5 watt AC-to-DC power converter that charges the battery in an hour or less. Indicator lights show when the battery needs charging and when it is fully charged. Model AT830 uses the newer HQ8 heads that provide somewhat closer shaves.<br /><br />Value-priced model 6948XL has a nickel-metal-hydride battery, has cutting heads mounted in a fixed holder and is not waterproof, providing only dry shaving. It connects directly to AC power. Its internal power converter takes a rated 8 hours to charge the battery. There are no battery indicator lights, so users guess when the battery needs charging and time the charges themselves. Model 6948XL uses the older HQ56 heads.<br /><br />The newer HQ8 heads each have two segments with fine, circular holes that are positioned toward the inside of a 3-head assembly. They are apparently intended to emulate the performance of foil shavers, handling short whiskers so that they are squarely cut. However, there are only 9 blades on an HQ8 cutter versus 15 blades on an older HQ56 cutter. To compensate, AT-series shavers rotate about 50 percent faster.<br /><br />Shave quality with model AT830 is good, if not quite as close as one gets from skillful use of a straight razor. It takes somewhat longer to get a uniform shave with model AT830 than with model 6948XL. Shave quality with model 6948XL is marginal, although it is better than one got with Norelco rotaries years ago. With either current Philips model, it takes less time to get uniform coverage of difficult neck and chin areas than it usually takes with a foil shaver.<br /><br />Philips rotaries have become value leaders among current electric shavers. Performance has improved over the Norelco rotary shavers of years ago--the brand Philips distributed in North America before the early 1980s. Philips currently offers models with good performance at premium, intermediate and value prices. Premium models have cutting heads mounted in floating holders and come with charging stands.<br /><br />I began using Remington electrics years ago, when they were the most reliable units of the day. In those days Norelco provided a shave with little skin irritation, but it was a fairly coarse shave with poor feel and appearance. Then Braun, while owned by Gillette, introduced titanium foil shavers that combined fairly close shaves with little skin irritation, and I switched to them.<br /><br />Unfortunately, foil shavers don't cope well with outlying areas of neck and chin, where whiskers tend to bend over and escape being clipped. The Braun triple-track design does better than just a curved foil, but it typically needs many passes to provide a uniform shave.<br /><br />With their high speeds, foil shavers don't really cut whiskers. They grind whiskers to powder, provided the whiskers can be persuaded through the holes in the surface of a foil. Currently Braun is delivering its best foil technology to the U.S. only at premium prices, encouraging another look at alternatives.<br /><br />Rotary shavers provide much of their action around the edges of disk-shaped \\"combs\\" where whiskers can slip through slots. Their low speeds encourage shaving with slower and more strategic motions. Because rotaries are quiet, one easily hears when cutters engage whiskers. Recent Philips models provide thinner combs and more precise mating of cutter blades to combs, as compared with Norelco models of years ago.<br /><br />Cleaning a rotary shaver appears more important than cleaning a foil shaver. Larger whisker fragments put drag on heads and internal parts. Removing head assemblies and brushing while dry has proved most effective, even though model AT830 can be washed with hot water. Philips does not offer cleaning accessories comparable to accessories from Braun. A few premium shavers have cleaning bases that can't be bought separately.<br /><br />Philips model AT830 is a good choice for everyday use at home. Overall, it performs as well or better than current foil shavers and provides uniform shaves somewhat faster. However, a little more time will be spent cleaning the shaver. Model 6948XL might be a good choice as a travel shaver. It's somewhat more rugged and won't cost as much to replace if lost or damaged.

  202. First of all, if you don't want a bunch of details, just scroll down to the IN SUMMARY paragraph at the end!<br /><br />I'm a longtime Norelco user, and the AT830 is a winner for me. Although I have a tough beard with hairs growing every which way, I have dealt with sensitive skin ever since I was a teenager. I learned a couple of decades ago that a rotary shaver that's made for use in the shower was my salvation. Thanks to Norelco wet-or-dry razors, I experience far less skin irritation. For me, having a good rotary shaver in the shower is indispensable. I know I'm not the only guy like this, so this is a detailed review for those of you who are considering an 810 or 830 model.<br /><br />I was glad to learn of the new Aquatec models, having used the Norelco 6000 and 7000 series Cool Skin razors for many years. For what it's worth, I tried the last wet/dry model (the 8060X) with the fully exposed shaving heads attached to a single stalk. After using it for a couple of weeks, I found that I couldn't get as close a shave as with my old 7735X model with the weakening battery. Also, the lack of a chamber for the clipped hair was inconvenient, so I returned it and went back to the old one.<br /><br />Upon learning of the newer Aquatec models, a friend (who's also a Norelco wet/dry fan) and I cooked up a plan. He also needed a new shaver thanks to a dying battery, so we both decided to buy a new model at the same time. He bought the slightly less expensive AT810, while I spent the extra 20 bucks for the 830. The only difference between the two is the \\"Smart Pivot\\" system on the 830, and I'd read mixed reviews as to whether it really mattered.<br /><br />THE TEST:<br />We each used our razors for one week, cleaned them properly with a good blade wash, then traded razors for a second week trial. We did not compare any notes until after going back to our own new shavers. I not only compared the new models to each other, but also compared these shaves to those Igot with my 7735X.<br /><br />Oh, and I tried one extra test once we got our original razors back after week two- I took my old 7735 out of retirement for one last shave. Granted, we aren't professional testers, but we tried to stay consistent in our testing. We both shaved just as we always did: in the morning before going to work. Both of us shave in the shower. The highly scientific test was for each of us to see how our shaves held up by 10 pm every night. Before anyone gripes, yes I know that Norelco says you need at least 21 days to try out a new razor. Well, here's what we found when we compared our observations after two weeks and two days. Your mileage may vary, as they say.<br /><br />RESULTS:<br />We both found that the AT830 gave a closer shave. No doubt about that; the pivot system did make a difference, since both models use the same HQ8 shaving heads. To be honest, the difference in closeness was greater for me, but I really do have a tougher beard. But by 10:00 each night, I noticed that I had a scratchier face of stubble using the 810. For me, the extra $20 was worth it. On the other hand, my pal felt that his model was fine for him, and he's keeping it.<br /><br />And how did my revisit with my old 7735X go after two weeks with the new models? It gave me a longer lasting shave than the 810 did, but not quite as long as the 830. If its battery weren't on the way out, I'd keep that one. However, I really like the fact that, unlike the 7000 series, the new models don't require a charging stand. The stand tips over easily and is an extra requirement to haul around when traveling.<br /><br />IN SUMMARY:<br />For those of you who didn't want to read my lengthy explanation, I totally understand! Anyhow, I found that, with my difficult beard, the AT830 was the way to go. I get a noticeably longer lasting shave than with the 810, and it slightly beats even my trusty old 7735X, which until now, no other razor could do. The 810, however, might be OK for anyone with a beard that's not so fussy. Either way, you'll get the closest, most comfortable shave in the shower with a good, low-foam shaving gel. I hope this helps someone who really has wanted to know the difference.

Normally I avoid Norelco because of their lift & cut system and fears it would generate more razor bumps.<br /><br />I purchased this product after comparing a competing product being used by black men and choose this one for its reliability after some reviews reported the competing product wore out after a year. From the first shave I made an effort to follow the instructions and do some experimentation and recommend other black men to do the same. Dry shaving doesn't work for me but the Aquatec feature allows me to use a small amount of shaving cream when I shave. I do have to rinse the trimmer heads with hot water when I shave, and I remove them to let them dry when I'm finished.<br /><br />Over the past month I discovered that getting the best shave from this product was about technique as much as it was about the product. I now shave every two and never more than three days, whereas before I could only manage to shave once a week. The floating heads of the Norelco allow me to painless shave over any razor bumps after I've lifted out any subcutaneous hairs. What I have found is that hair on my beard is normally straight out on day two, resulting in a nice close shave.<br /><br />So after nearly a month of using this product, I highly recommend it for any other black man who likes a close shave. In my case it doesn't eliminate razor bumps, but it also doesn't make my face any worse. In case it helps someone else here's my shaving process.<br /><br />1. Buff an exfoliation pad to remove dry skin and lift some hairs.<br />2. Using a sterilized safety pin, lift ingrown hairs out of the skin. Only pulling loose hairs with tweezers. If a hair is lose it slides right out by the way.<br />3. Wet my face and apply a thin film of shaving cream to serve as a skin lubricant.<br />4. Shave by letting the razor glide over the skin, making circular motions, and avoid pushing the razor against the skin.<br />5. Rinse the heads often with hot water and rinse clean when done, removing the head assembly so it will completely dry.<br />6. Wash face and apply a shaving lotion.<br /><br />The above steps are what works for me so I don't expect it to work for everyone. I do encourage you to give this product a serious try, especially if you are a professional black man.tweezers. If a hair is lose it slides right out by the way.<br />3. It's much more comfortable, near zero razor burn and is probably about as close as you can get (no pun intended) to a good blade setup. Cleanup is a breeze just push the button to flip open the top and rinse under running water, done. No more fiddling with little brushes and whisker dust.<br /><br />The heads have both the traditional slots that Norelco has been using forever and also a section with little holes. I assume this is to mimick a foil shaver, perhaps give the best of both worlds. Quick charges in 1 hour, a nice feature over the traditional 8 hour charge cycles but one that is mandatory I think for a razor that can't be used when plugged in (see comments below).<br /><br />The LED indicators are an essential addition IMO for battery and charge status. It's nice Norelco brought this back for their lower priced line as in previous product generations only the most high end shavers costing hundreds included indicator lights. And I'm glad they finally have moved their battery chemistry into the modern age of lipo batteries. So no more memory issues with NiCad or NiMh and lipo has better performance than either of those two.<br /><br />The only downside to this razor is it can't be used when plugged in for safety reasons I presume since it can be used in the shower. While I have no desire to be electrocuted, it means that once the batteries die in this unit you'll either have to buy another shaver, or try to replace the batteries yourself which is a daunting task requiring disassembly, working with really small parts, soldering skills and breaking the water seal but it can be done. But with a 2-1/2 year warranty you should be covered and after that it's probably time for a new one anyway.e anyway.

  641. In some respects, the more Norelco shavers change, the more they stay the same. They all still use the same basic rotary blade sets...because they work really well. What has changed is:<br />1. How they get power (a battery).<br />2. What else you can do with them (shave in the shower and/or with shaving gel).<br /><br />Battery power is a great convenience, but only if the battery lasts a long time and is easy to charge. I bought this model because it strikes the best balance of shaving/charging time to price.<br /><br />This Norelco charges in less than an hour and the charge goes for two weeks, at least when the shaver is new. The other feature that I like, but haven't been able to confirm from the manual, is that the razor seems to cut off charging automatically when its fully charged. If you don't overcharge the battery it lasts longer and you'll be happier. Automatic shut-off is one more thing in life that you don't have to pay attention to.<br /><br />I bought this model because I was intrigued by the tilting shave head. I'm not convinced it was worth the additional $10 over the next lower model. Both have the same battery and the same shave/charge characteristiscs that are most important to me. The tilting head might help, but I haven't noticed that it gives me a better shave.<br /><br />Norelco wants you to replace the rotary blade sets every year. In my experience, that's not necessary. Rinse the head from the inside out a couple times a week. Take the rotary cutters out of the head a couple times a year, soak them in alcohol, then put them back in, making sure that you put the cutters back in the same screens. You'll get a good shave for three years or more. The battery will wear out before the blades do.<br /><br />Wet shaving? Gel? Why? If I wanted a wet shave, I'd use a blade. But it is nice to have a water-resistant shaver that you can wash vigorously without having to worry about drowning it.<br /><br />One note about all types of shavers and razors.Every time you switch from one to another, it takes a week or two for your skin to adjust.
